[157] ✓ CORRECT
  Question: My symptoms are yellowish skin, vomiting, high fever, weight loss, fatigue, dark urine, abdominal pain, and itching. What could this be?
  True Answer: Jaundice
  Predicted: Jaundice
 Jaundice is a condition in which there is a high level of bilirubin in the blood. Bilirubin is a yellow pigment formed when red blood cells are broken down. The excessive bilirubin is excreted by the liver into the bile ducts and the stool. The yellowish skin, dark urine, fatigue, and abdominal pain are characteristic of this condition.

[348] ✓ CORRECT
  Question: I have these symptoms: fatigue, yellowish skin, family history, nausea, loss of appetite, and yellowing of eyes. What do I have?
  True Answer: Hepatitis C
  Predicted: Hepatitis C

 Explanation: Hepatitis C is a blood-borne viral infection that causes liver inflammation and sometimes leads to liver damage and even liver cancer or death. It is spread by contact with infected blood. Hepatitis C can have no symptoms, or it may present with fatigue, nausea, loss of appetite, yellowing of eyes, and family history. It is important to get tested if you have a high-risk profile or have been exposed to the virus.

[481] ✓ CORRECT
  Question: I have these symptoms: headache, chills, muscle pain, diarrhoea, vomiting, sweating, nausea, and high fever. What do I have?
  True Answer: Malaria
  Predicted: Malaria
 Malaria is a blood borne parasitic infection spread by the bite of an infected Anopheles mosquito. Malaria is classified into uncomplicated and complicated forms. Complicated malaria is further classified into severe and coma. Malaria can lead to complications such as kidney failure, liver failure, yellowish skin, respiratory distress, brain damage, and death.

[592] ✓ CORRECT
  Question: My symptoms are lethargy, abdominal pain, malaise, dark urine, itching, receiving blood transfusion, loss of appetite, receiving unsterile injections, yellow urine, yellowing of eyes, yellowish skin, and fatigue. What could this be?
  True Answer: Hepatitis B
  Predicted: Hepatitis B

 Treatment: For acute hepatitis B, stopping alcohol consumption, avoiding fatty and spicy foods, and taking rest are recommended. The prognosis of hepatitis B is good and it usually does not lead to chronicity. Patients with chronic hepatitis B are treated with interferon, which suppresses the virus in many patients. Liver transplantation is the last resort for patients with liver cirrhosis and end-stage liver disease.

[866] ✓ CORRECT
  Question: I have these symptoms: dark urine, yellowing of eyes, nausea, fatigue, yellowish skin, vomiting, abdominal pain, and loss of appetite. What do I have?
  True Answer: Hepatitis D
  Predicted: Hepatitis D
Hepatitis D is a liver disease caused by the hepatitis D virus. It is considered a second-wave disease, meaning it emerged after the initial outbreak of hepatitis B. It is similar to hepatitis B and is usually caused in conjunction with it. The disease is the result of a coinfection with both the hepatitis B and hepatitis D viruses. Hepatitis D is a rare disease, encountered mainly in patients who are carriers of the hepatitis B virus.

[1128] ✓ CORRECT
  Question: My symptoms are brittle nails, lethargy, fatigue, puffy face and eyes, mood swings, cold hands and feets, swollen extremeties, abnormal menstruation, irritability, enlarged thyroid, dizziness, weight gain, and depression. What could this be?
  True Answer: Hypothyroidism
  Predicted: Hypothyroidism

Hyperthyroidism and hypothyroidism are two conditions that are commonly confused as they have similar symptoms. Hypothyroidism is a condition where the thyroid gland does not produce enough thyroid hormone. This condition is typically diagnosed by an elevated thyroid-stimulating hormone (TSH) level and a low free thyroid hormone level. Physical examination and blood tests are normal in this condition.

[1173] ✓ CORRECT
  Question: My symptoms are lack of concentration, headache, dizziness, and chest pain. What could this be?
  True Answer: Hypertension 
  Predicted: Hypertension 

 Hypertension is a condition in which blood pressure is consistently elevated. Blood pressure is the force of your heartbeat against the walls of your arteries. Each heartbeat pushes the blood from your heart to your arteries at a higher pressure, and then when your heart rests, the pressure in your arteries falls. If the pressure remains elevated over time, it can cause many serious health problems.
